href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>.</div></div></div></div>
<p>January 2013, Cisco Systems acquired Israeli software maker Intucell for around $475 million in cash, a move to expand its mobile network management offerings.<sup id="cite_ref-Cisco-Feb-2013-10-Q_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cisco-Feb-2013-10-Q-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> In the same month, Cisco Systems acquired Cognitive Security, a company focused on Cyber Threat Protection. Cisco also acquired SolveDirect (cloud services) in March 2013<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> and Ubiquisys (mobile software) in April 2013.
</p><p>Cisco acquired cyber-security firm <a href="/wiki/Sourcefire" title="Sourcefire">Sourcefire</a>, in October 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup>
On June 16, 2014, Cisco announced that it has completed the acquisition of ThreatGRID, a company that provided dynamic malware analysis and threat intelligence technology.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p><p>June 17, 2014, Cisco announced its intent to acquire privately held Tail-f Systems, a leader in multi-vendor network service orchestration solutions for traditional and virtualized networks.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p><p>April 2, 2015, Cisco announced plans to buy Embrane, a software-defined networking startup. The deal will give Cisco Embrane's software platform, which provides layer 3–7 network services for things such as firewalls, VPN termination, server load balancers and SSL offload.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p><p>May 7, 2015 Cisco announced plans to buy Tropo, a cloud API platform that simplifies the addition of real-time communications and collaboration capabilities within applications.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p><p>June 30, 2015, Cisco acquired privately-held <a href="/wiki/OpenDNS" title="OpenDNS">OpenDNS</a>, the company best known for its DNS service that adds a level of security by monitoring domain name requests.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p><p>August 6, 2015, Cisco announced that it has completed the acquisition of privately held MaintenanceNet, the US-based company best known for its cloud-based contract management platform ServiceExchange.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> On the same month, Cisco acquired Pawaa, a privately held company in Bangalore, India that provides secure on-premises and cloud-based file-sharing software.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p><p>September 30, 2015, Cisco announced its intent to acquire privately held Portcullis Computer Security, a UK-based company that provides cybersecurity services to enterprise clients and the government sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p><p>October 26, 2015, Cisco announced its intent to acquire ParStream, a privately held company based in Cologne, Germany, that provides an analytics database that allows companies to analyze large amounts of data and store it in near real-time anywhere in the network.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p><p>October 27, 2015, Cisco announced that it would acquire <a href="/wiki/Lancope" class="mw-redirect" title="Lancope">Lancope</a>, a company that focuses on detecting threat activity, for $452.5 million in a cash-and-equity deal.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p><p>June 28, 2016, Cisco announced its intent to acquire CloudLock, a privately held cloud security company founded in 2011 by three <a href="/wiki/Israeli_military" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli military">Israeli military</a> veterans,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> for $293 million.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The deal was expected to close in the first quarter of 2017.
</p><p>In August 2016, Cisco announced it is getting closer to making a deal to acquire Springpath, the startup whose technology is used in Cisco's HyperFlex Systems. Cisco already owns an undisclosed stake in the hyper-converged provider.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p><p>January 2017, Cisco announced they would acquire <a href="/wiki/AppDynamics" title="AppDynamics">AppDynamics</a>, a company that monitors application performance, for $3.7 billion. The acquisition came just one day before AppDynamics was set to IPO.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p><p>January 26, 2017, Cisco founded the Innovation Alliance in Germany with eleven other companies bringing together 40 sites and 2,000 staff to provide small businesses in Germany with expertise.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p><p>August 1, 2017, Cisco completed the acquisition of Viptela Inc. for $610 million in cash and assumed equity awards.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>  Viptela was a privately held software-defined wide area network (SD-WAN) company based in San Jose, Ca.
</p><p>October 23, 2017, Cisco Systems announced it would be acquiring Broadsoft for $1.9 Billion to further entrench itself in the cloud communication and collaboration area.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ownership" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>As of 2017 Cisco Systems shares are mainly held by institutional investors (<a href="/wiki/The_Vanguard_Group" title="The Vanguard Group">The Vanguard Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/BlackRock" title="BlackRock">BlackRock</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_Street_Corporation" title="State Street Corporation">State Street Corporation</a> and others<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>)
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Products_and_services">Products and services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Products and services" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Cisco_products" title="List of Cisco products">List of Cisco products</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r923042769/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Cisco_small_business_SG300-28_28-port_Gigabit_Ethernet_rackmount_switch.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Cisco_small_business_SG300-28_28-port_Gigabit_Ethernet_rackmount_switch.jpg/200px-Cisco_small_business_SG300-28_28-port_Gigabit_Ethernet_rackmount_switch.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 150px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Cisco_small_business_SG300-28_28-port_Gigabit_Ethernet_rackmount_switch.jpg/200px-Cisco_small_business_SG300-28_28-port_Gigabit_Ethernet_rackmount_switch.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="150"> </span></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Cisco_Model_EPC3010.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Cisco_Model_EPC3010.jpg/200px-Cisco_Model_EPC3010.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 133px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Cisco_Model_EPC3010.jpg/200px-Cisco_Model_EPC3010.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="133"> </span></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="thumbcaption" style="background-color:transparent">Cisco SG300-28 Rackmount switch (top) and Cisco EPC-3010 modem (bottom).</div></div></div></div>
<p>Cisco's products and services focus upon three market segments—enterprise, service provider, midsize and small business.
</p><p>Cisco provides IT products and services across five major technology areas:  Networking (including Ethernet, optical, wireless and mobility), Security, Collaboration (including voice, video, and data), Data Center, and the Internet of Things.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p><p>Cisco has grown increasingly popular in the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific" title="Asia-Pacific">Asia-Pacific</a> region over the last three decades<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2015)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> and is the dominant vendor in the Australian market with <a href="/wiki/Leadership" title="Leadership">leadership</a> across all market segments.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It uses its Australian office as one of the main headquarters for the Asia-Pacific region.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="VoIP_services">VoIP services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: VoIP services" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Cisco became a major provider of <a href="/wiki/Voice_over_IP" title="Voice over IP">Voice over IP</a> to enterprises and is now moving into the home user market through its acquisitions of Scientific Atlanta and Linksys. Scientific Atlanta provides VoIP equipment to cable service providers such as <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner" class="mw-redirect" title="Time Warner">Time Warner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cablevision" title="Cablevision">Cablevision</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Communications" title="Rogers Communications">Rogers Communications</a>, UPC and others; Linksys has partnered with companies such as <a href="/wiki/Skype" title="Skype">Skype</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a> to integrate consumer VoIP services with wireless and cordless phones.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Hosted_Collaboration_Solution_.28HCS.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hosted_Collaboration_Solution_(HCS)">Hosted Collaboration Solution (HCS)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Hosted Collaboration Solution (HCS)" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Cisco partners can offer cloud-based services based on Cisco's virtualized <a href="/wiki/Cisco_Unified_Computing_System" title="Cisco Unified Computing System">Unified Computing System</a> (UCS). A part of the Cisco Unified Services Delivery Solution that includes hosted versions of Cisco Unified Communications Manager (UCM), Cisco Unified Contact Center, Cisco Unified Mobility, Cisco Unified Presence, Cisco Unity Connection (unified messaging) and Cisco Webex Meeting Center.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Network_Emergency_Response">Network Emergency Response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Network Emergency Response" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cisco_8851.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Cisco_8851.JPG/200px-Cisco_8851.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 133px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Cisco_8851.JPG/200px-Cisco_8851.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="133" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cisco_8851.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Cisco 8851 IP Phone</div></div></div>
<p>As part of its Tactical Operations initiative, Cisco maintains several Network Emergency Response Vehicles (NERV)s.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-121">[121]</a></sup> The vehicles are maintained and deployed by Cisco employees during natural disasters and other public crises. The vehicles are self-contained and provide wired and wireless services including voice and radio interoperability, voice over IP, network-based video surveillance and secured high-definition video-conferencing for <a href="/wiki/Leader" class="mw-redirect" title="Leader">leaders</a> and first responders in crisis areas with up to 3 Mbit/s of bandwidth (up and down) via a 1.8-meter satellite antenna.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p><p>NERVs are based at Cisco headquarters sites in <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose, California</a> and at Research Triangle Park, North Carolina, allowing strategic deployment in North America. They can become fully operational within 15 minutes of arrival. High-capacity diesel fuel-tanks allow the largest vehicles to run for up to 72 hours continuously.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> The NERV has been deployed to incidents such as the <a href="/wiki/October_2007_California_wildfires" title="October 2007 California wildfires">October 2007 California wildfires</a>; hurricanes <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gustav" title="Hurricane Gustav">Gustav</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ike" title="Hurricane Ike">Ike</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Katrina</a>; the <a href="/wiki/2010_San_Bruno_pipeline_explosion" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 San Bruno pipeline explosion">2010 San Bruno gas pipeline explosion</a>, tornado outbreaks in <a href="/wiki/Tornado_outbreak_of_April_14%E2%80%9316,_2011" title="Tornado outbreak of April 14–16, 2011">North Carolina</a> and <a href="/wiki/2011_Super_Outbreak" title="2011 Super Outbreak">Alabama</a> in 2011; and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">Hurricane Sandy</a> in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p><p>The Tactical Operations team maintains and deploys smaller, more portable communication kits to emergencies outside of North America. In 2010, the team deployed to assist in earthquake recovery in Haiti and Christchurch (New Zealand). In 2011, they deployed to flooding in Brazil, as well as in response to the 2011 earthquake and tsunami in Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-121">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p><p>In 2011, Cisco received the Innovation Preparedness award from the <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">American Red Cross</a> Silicon Valley Chapter for its development and use of these vehicles in disasters.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Certifications">Certifications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Certifications" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cisco_certifications" title="Cisco certifications">Cisco certifications</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciscosystemsheadquarters.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Ciscosystemsheadquarters.jpg/200px-Ciscosystemsheadquarters.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="154" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1381" data-file-height="1063"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 154px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Ciscosystemsheadquarters.jpg/200px-Ciscosystemsheadquarters.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="154" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciscosystemsheadquarters.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cisco headquarters in the <a href="/wiki/North_San_Jose_Innovation_District" title="North San Jose Innovation District">North San Jose Innovation District</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose, California</a> in <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Cisco Systems also sponsors a line of <a href="/wiki/Professional_certification_(computer_technology)" title="Professional certification (computer technology)">IT professional certifications</a> for Cisco products.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> There are four or five (path to <a href="/wiki/Network_planning_and_design" title="Network planning and design">network designers</a>) levels of certification: Entry (CCENT), Associate (<a href="/wiki/Cisco_CCNA" class="mw-redirect" title="Cisco CCNA">CCNA</a>/CCDA), Professional (CCNP/CCDP), Expert (CCIE/CCDE) and recently Architect (CCAr: CCDE previous),<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> as well as nine different paths, Routing &amp; Switching, Design, Industrial Network, Network Security, Service Provider, Service Provider Operations, Storage Networking, Voice, Datacenter and Wireless.
</p><p>A number of specialist technicians, sales and datacenter certifications are also available.
</p><p>Cisco also provides training for these certifications via a portal called the Cisco Networking Academy. Qualifying schools can become members of the Cisco Networking Academy and then provide CCNA level or other level courses. Cisco Academy Instructors must be CCNA certified to be a CCAI certified instructor.
</p><p>Cisco often finds itself involved with technical education. With over 10,000 partnerships in over 65 countries<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Cisco Academy program operates in many exotic locations. For example, in March 2013, Cisco announced its interest in <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> by investing in two Cisco Networking Academies in <a href="/wiki/Yangon" title="Yangon">Yangon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mandalay" title="Mandalay">Mandalay</a> and a channel partner network.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_accolades">Awards and accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Awards and accolades" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Embassy_Tel_Aviv_-_ACE_3.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/US_Embassy_Tel_Aviv_-_ACE_3.jpg/220px-US_Embassy_Tel_Aviv_-_ACE_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="799"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 146px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/US_Embassy_Tel_Aviv_-_ACE_3.jpg/220px-US_Embassy_Tel_Aviv_-_ACE_3.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="146" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Embassy_Tel_Aviv_-_ACE_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 2010, Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> awarded Cisco the Secretary of State's Award for Corporate Excellence, which was presented in <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> by Ambassador <a href="/wiki/James_B._Cunningham" title="James B. Cunningham">James B. Cunningham</a> to Cisco Senior Manager Zika Abzuk.</div></div></div>
<p>Cisco products, including IP phones and Telepresence, have been seen in movies and TV series.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> The company was featured in the documentary film <i><a href="/wiki/Something_Ventured" title="Something Ventured">Something Ventured</a></i> which premiered in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p><p>Cisco was a 2002–03 recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Ron_Brown_Award" title="Ron Brown Award">Ron Brown Award</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> a U.S. presidential honor to recognize companies "for the exemplary quality of their relationships with employees and communities". In 2020, <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i> magazine ranked Cisco Systems at number four on their Fortune List of the Top 100 Companies to Work For in 2020 based on an employee survey of satisfaction.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p><p>According to a report by technology consulting firm <a href="/wiki/LexInnova_Technologies" title="LexInnova Technologies">LexInnova</a>, Cisco was one of the leading recipients of network security-related patents with the largest portfolio within other companies (6,442 security-related patents) in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Controversies" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cisco_Networkers_2007_-_Anaheim.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Cisco_Networkers_2007_-_Anaheim.JPG/220px-Cisco_Networkers_2007_-_Anaheim.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Cisco_Networkers_2007_-_Anaheim.JPG/220px-Cisco_Networkers_2007_-_Anaheim.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cisco_Networkers_2007_-_Anaheim.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cisco Live 2007 in <a href="/wiki/Anaheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Anaheim">Anaheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>. Cisco Live is the company's annual exposition and conference.</div></div></div>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Shareholder_relations">Shareholder relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Shareholder relations" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>A class action lawsuit filed on April 20, 2001, accused Cisco of making misleading statements that "were relied on by purchasers of Cisco stock" and of <a href="/wiki/Insider_trading" title="Insider trading">insider trading</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> While Cisco denied all allegations in the suit, on August 18, 2006, Cisco's liability insurers, its directors and officers paid the plaintiffs US$91.75 million to settle the suit.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Intellectual_property_disputes">Intellectual property disputes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Intellectual property disputes" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>On December 11, 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Free_Software_Foundation" title="Free Software Foundation">Free Software Foundation</a> <a href="/wiki/FSF_vs._Cisco" class="mw-redirect" title="FSF vs. Cisco">filed suit against Cisco</a> regarding Cisco's failure to comply with the <a href="/wiki/GPL" class="mw-redirect" title="GPL">GPL</a> and <a href="/wiki/LGPL" class="mw-redirect" title="LGPL">LGPL</a> license models and make the applicable source code publicly available.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> On May 20, 2009, Cisco settled this lawsuit by complying with FSF licensing terms and making a monetary contribution to the FSF.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Censorship_in_China">Censorship in China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Censorship in China" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Cisco has been criticized for its involvement in <a href="/wiki/Censorship_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Censorship in the People's Republic of China">censorship in the People's Republic of China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> According to author <a href="/wiki/Ethan_Gutmann" title="Ethan Gutmann">Ethan Gutmann</a>, Cisco and other telecommunications equipment providers supplied the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">Chinese government</a> with surveillance and Internet infrastructure equipment that is used to block Internet websites and track online activities in China.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> Cisco has stated that it does not customize or develop specialized or unique filtering capabilities to enable governments to block access to information and that it sells the same equipment in China as it sells worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Wired_News" class="mw-redirect" title="Wired News">Wired News</a> had uncovered a leaked, confidential Cisco PowerPoint presentation that detailed the commercial opportunities of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Shield_Project" title="Golden Shield Project">Golden Shield Project</a> of Internet control.<sup id="cite_ref-Stirland_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stirland-145">[145]</a></sup> In May 2011, a group of <a href="/wiki/Falun_Gong" title="Falun Gong">Falun Gong</a> practitioners filed a lawsuit under the <a href="/wiki/Alien_Tort_Statute" title="Alien Tort Statute">Alien Tort Statute</a> alleging that Cisco knowingly developed and customized its product to assist the Chinese government in prosecution and abuse of <a href="/wiki/Falun_Gong" title="Falun Gong">Falun Gong</a> practitioners.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The lawsuit was dismissed in September 2014<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Northern_District_of_California" title="United States District Court for the Northern District of California">United States District Court for the Northern District of California</a>, which decision was appealed to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Ninth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit">United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit</a><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> in September 2015.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Tax_fraud_investigation">Tax fraud investigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tax fraud investigation" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In October 2007, employees of Cisco's Brazilian unit were arrested on charges that they had imported equipment without paying import duties. In response, Cisco stated that they do not import directly into Brazil, and instead use middlemen.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Antitrust_lawsuit">Antitrust lawsuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Antitrust lawsuit" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>On December 1, 2008, <a href="/wiki/Multiven" title="Multiven">Multiven</a> filed an <a href="/wiki/Antitrust" class="mw-redirect" title="Antitrust">antitrust</a> lawsuit<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> against Cisco Systems, Inc. Multiven's complaint alleges that Cisco harmed Multiven and consumers by bundling and <a href="/wiki/Tying_(commerce)" title="Tying (commerce)">tying</a> <a href="/wiki/Software_bug" title="Software bug">bug</a> fixes/<a href="/wiki/Patch_(computing)" title="Patch (computing)">patches</a> and updates for its <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating system</a> software to its maintenance services (SMARTnet). In May 2010, Cisco accused the person who filed the <a href="/wiki/Antitrust" class="mw-redirect" title="Antitrust">antitrust</a> suit, British-Nigerian technology entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Peter_Alfred-Adekeye" class="mw-redirect" title="Peter Alfred-Adekeye">Peter Alfred-Adekeye</a>, with hacking and pressured the US government to extradite him from Canada. Cisco settled the antitrust lawsuit two months after Alfred-Adekeye's arrest by making its software updates available to all Multiven customers.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span id="Remotely_monitoring_users.27_connections"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Remotely_monitoring_users'_connections">Remotely monitoring users' connections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Remotely monitoring users' connections" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Cisco's Linksys E2700, E3500, E4500 devices have been reported to be remotely updated to a firmware version that forces users to register for a cloud service, allows Cisco to monitor their network use and ultimately shut down the cloud service account and thus render the affected router unusable.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Firewall_backdoor_developed_by_NSA">Firewall backdoor developed by NSA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Firewall backdoor developed by NSA" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>According to the German magazine <a href="/wiki/Der_Spiegel" title="Der Spiegel">Der Spiegel</a> the NSA has developed JETPLOW for gaining access to ASA (series 5505, 5510, 5520, 5540 and 5550) and 500-series PIX Firewalls.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p><p>Cisco's Chief Security Officer addressed the allegations publicly and denied working with any government to weaken Cisco products for exploitation or to implement security back doors.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p><p>A document included in the trove of National Security Agency files released with Glenn Greenwald's book <i>No Place to Hide</i> details how the agency's <a href="/wiki/Tailored_Access_Operations" title="Tailored Access Operations">Tailored Access Operations</a> (TAO) unit and other NSA employees intercept servers, routers and other network gear being shipped to organizations targeted for surveillance and install covert firmware onto them before they are delivered. These Trojan horse systems were described by an NSA manager as being “some of the most productive operations in TAO because they pre-position access points into hard target networks around the world.”<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p><p>Cisco denied the allegations in a customer document<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> saying that no information was included about specific Cisco products, supply chain intervention or implant techniques, or new security vulnerabilities. Cisco's general counsel also said that Cisco does not work with any government, including the United States Government, to weaken its products.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> The allegations are reported to have prompted the company's CEO to express concern to the President of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Spherix_patent_suit">Spherix patent suit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Spherix patent suit" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In March 2014 Cisco Systems was sued for patent infringement. Spherix says that over $43 billion of Cisco's sales infringe on old <a href="/wiki/Nortel" title="Nortel">Nortel</a> patents owned by Spherix. Officials with Spherix are saying that a wide range of Cisco products, from switches to routers, infringe on 11 former Nortel patents that the company now owns.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="India_Net_censorship_role">India Net censorship role</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cisco_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: India Net censorship role" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Cisco Systems will help the Indian administration build a firewall that will prevent Internet users in <a href="/wiki/Kashmir" title="Kashmir">Kashmir</a> from accessing blacklisted websites, including social media portals, through fixed-line connections.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
